\tchanges.AppendResourceInstanceChange(csrc)\n570: \tif deposedKey == states.NotDeposed {\n571: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] writeChange: recorded %s change for %s\", change.Action, n.Addr)\n572: \t} else {\n573: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] writeChange: recorded %s change for %s deposed object %s\", change.Action, n.Addr, deposedKey)\n574: \t}\n575: \n576: \treturn nil\n577: }\n578: \n579: // refresh does a refresh for a resource\n580: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) refresh(ctx EvalContext, deposedKey states.DeposedKey, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject) (*states.ResourceInstanceObject, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n581: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n582: \tabsAddr := n.Addr\n583: \tif deposedKey == states.NotDeposed {\n584: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] NodeAbstractResourceInstance.refresh providerSchema.SchemaForResourceAddr(n.Addr.Resource.ContainingResource())\n599: \tif schema == nil {\n600: \t\t// Should be caught during validation, so we don't bother with a pretty error here\n601: \t}\n618: \n619: \t// Refresh!\n620: \tpriorVal := state.Value\n621: \n622: \t// Unmarked before sending to provider\n623: \tvar priorPaths []cty.PathValueMarks\n624: \tif priorVal.ContainsMarked() {\n625: \t\tpriorVal, priorPaths = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n626: \t}\n627: \n628: \tvar resp providers.ReadResourceResponse\n629: \tif n.override != nil {\n630: \t\t// If we have an override set for this resource, we don't want to talk\n631: \t\t// to the provider so we'll just return whatever was in state.\n632: \t\tresp = providers.ReadResourceResponse{\n633: \t\t\tNewState: priorVal,\n634: \t\t}\n635: \t} else {\n636: \t\tresp = provider.ReadResource(providers.ReadResourceRequest{\n637: \t\t\tTypeName:     n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n638: \t\t\tPriorState: \t}\n651: \n652: \tif resp.NewState == cty.NilVal {\n653: \t\t// This ought not to happen in real cases since it's not possible to\n654: \t\t// send NilVal over the plugin RPC channel, but it can come during refresh: %s.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n676: \t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, absAddr, ret, diags\n723: }\n724: \n725: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) plan(\n726: \tctx EvalContext,\n727: \tplannedChange *plans.ResourceInstanceChange,\n728: \tcurrentState *states.ResourceInstanceObject,\n729: \tcreateBeforeDestroy bool,\n730: \tforceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance,\n731: ) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, *states.ResourceInstanceObject, instances.RepetitionData, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n732: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n733: \tvar keyData instances.RepetitionData\n734: \n735: \tresource := n.Addr.Resource.Resource\n736: \tprovider, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n737: \tif err != nil {\n738: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags.Append(err)\n739: \t}\n740: \n741: \tschema, _ := generate it now.\n749: \tif n.Config == nil {\n750: \t\t// This shouldn't happen. A node that isn't generating config should\n751: \t\t// have embedded config, and the rest of Terraform should enforce this.\n752: \t\t// If, however, we didn't do things correctly the next line will panic,\n753: \t\t// so let's not do that and return an error message with more context.\n754: \n755: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n756: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n757: \t\t\t\"Resource has no configuration\",\n758: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"Terraform attempted to process a resource at %s that has no configuration. This is a bug in Terraform; please report it!\", n.Addr.String())))\n759: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n760: \t}\n761: \n762: \tconfig := *n.Config\n763: \n764: \tcheckRuleSeverity := tfdiags.Error\n765: \tif n.preDestroyRefresh {\n766: \t\tcheckRuleSeverity = tfdiags.Warning\n767: \t}\n768: \n769: \tif plannedChange != nil {\n770: \t\t// If we already planned the action, we stick to that plan\n771: \t\tcreateBeforeDestroy = plannedChange.Action == plans.CreateThenDelete\n772: \t}\n773: \n774: \t// Evaluate the configuration\n775: \tforEach, _ := evaluateForEachExpression(n.Config.ForEach, ctx)\n776: \n777: \tkeyData = EvalDataForInstanceKey(n.ResourceInstanceAddr().Resource.Key, forEach)\n778: \n779: \tcheckDiags := evalCheckRules(\n780: \t\taddrs.ResourcePrecondition,\n781: \t\tn.Config.Preconditions,\n782: \t\tctx, n.Addr, keyData,\n783: \t\tcheckRuleSeverity,\n784: \t)\n785: \tdiags = diags.Append(checkDiags)\n786: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n787: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags // failed preconditions prevent further evaluation\n788: \t}\n789: \n790: \t// If we have a previous plan and the action was a noop, then the only\n791: \t// reason we're in this method was to evaluate the preconditions. There's\n792: \t// no need to re-plan this resource.\n793: \tif plannedChange != nil && plannedChange.Action == plans.NoOp {\n794: \t\treturn plannedChange, currentState.DeepCopy(), keyData, diags\n795: \t}\n796: \n797: \torigConfigVal, _, configDiags := ctx.EvaluateBlock(config.Config, schema, nil, keyData)\n798: \tdiags = diags.Append(configDiags)\n799: \tif configDiags.HasErrors() {\n800: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n801: \t}\n802: \n803: \tmetaConfigVal, metaDiags := n.providerMetas(ctx)\n804: \tdiags = diags.Append(metaDiags)\n805: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n806: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n807: \t}\n808: \n809: \tvar priorVal cty.Value\n810: \tvar priorValTainted cty.Value\n811: \tvar priorPrivate []byte\n812: \tif currentState != nil {\n813: \t\tif currentState.Status != states.ObjectTainted {\n814: \t\t\tpriorVal = currentState.Value\n815: \t\t\tpriorPrivate = currentState.Private\n816: \t\t} else {\n817: \t\t\t// If the prior state is tainted then we'll proceed below like\n818: \t\t\t// we're creating an entirely new object, but then turn it into\n819: \t\t\t// a synthetic \"Replace\" change at the end, creating the same\n820: \t\t\t// result as if the provider had marked at least one argument\n821: \t\t\t// change as \"requires replacement\".\n822: \t\t\tpriorValTainted = currentState.Value\n823: \t\t\tpriorVal = cty.NullVal(schema.ImpliedType())\n824: \t\t}\n825: \t} else {\n826: \t\tpriorVal = cty.NullVal(schema.ImpliedType())\n827: \t}\n828: \n829: \tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] Re-validating config for %q\", n.Addr)\n830: \t// Allow the provider to validate the final set of values.  The config was\n831: \t// statically validated early on, but there may have been unknown values\n832: \t// which the provider could not validate at the time.\n833: \t//\n834: \t// TODO: It would be more correct to validate the config after\n835: \t// ignore_changes has been applied, but the current implementation cannot\n836: \t// exclude computed-only attributes when given the `all` option.\n837: \n838: \t// we must unmark and use the original config, since the ignore_changes\n839: \t// handling below needs access to the marks.\n840: \tunmarkedConfigVal, _ := origConfigVal.UnmarkDeep()\n841: \tvalidateResp := provider.ValidateResourceConfig(\n842: \t\tproviders.ValidateResourceConfigRequest{\n843: \t\t\tTypeName: n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n844: \t\t\tConfig:   unmarkedConfigVal,\n845: \t\t},\n846: \t)\n847: \tdiags = diags.Append(validateResp.Diagnostics.InConfigBody(config.Config, n.Addr.String()))\n848: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n849: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n850: \t}\n851: \n852: \t// ignore_changes is meant to only apply to the configuration, so it must\n853: \t// be applied before we generate a plan. Since real-world providers return via RPC a nil\n921: \t\t// is always a bug in the client-side stub. This is more likely caused\n922: \t\t// by an incompletely-configured mock provider in tests, though.\n923: \t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"PlanResourceChange of %s produced nil value\", n.Addr))\n924: \t}\n925: \n926: \t// We allow the planned new value to disagree with configuration _values_\n927: \t// here, since that allows the provider to do special logic like a\n928: \t// DiffSuppressFunc, but for %s.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n936: \t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, tfdiags.FormatErrorPrefixed(err, n.Addr.String()),\n937: \t\t\t),\n938: \t\t))\n939: \t}\n940: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n941: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n942: \t}\n943: \n944: \tif errs := objchange.AssertPlanValid(schema, unmarkedPriorVal, unmarkedConfigVal, plannedNewVal); len(errs) > 0 {\n945: \t\tif resp.LegacyTypeSystem {\n946: \t\t\t// The shimming of the old type system in the legacy SDK is not precise\n947: \t\t\t// enough to pass this consistency check, so we'll give it a pass here,\n948: \t\t\t// but we will generate a warning about it so that we are more likely\n949: \t\t\t// to notice in the logs if tfdiags.FormatError(err))\n958: \t\t\t}\n959: \t\t\tlog.Print(buf.String())\n960: \t\t} else {\n961: \t\t\tfor _, err := range errs {\n962: \t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n963: provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n967: \t\t\t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, tfdiags.FormatErrorPrefixed(err, n.Addr.String()),\n968: \t\t\t\t\t),\n969: contract and\n977: \t\t// return changes to non-computed values, the plan response may have\n978: \t\t// altered values that were already suppressed with ignore_changes.\n979: \t\t// A prime example of this is where providers attempt to obfuscate\n980: \t\t// config data by turning the config value into a hash and storing the\n981: \t\t// hash value in the state. There are enough cases of this in existing\n982: \t\t// providers that we must accommodate the behavior for now, so for\n983: \t\t// ignore_changes to work at all on these values, we will revert the\n984: \t\t// ignored values once more.\n985: \t\t// A nil schema is passed to processIgnoreChanges to indicate that we\n986: \t\t// don't want to fixup a config value according to the schema plannedNewVal.MarkWithPaths(unmarkedPaths)\n1000: \t}\n1001: \n1002: \t// The provider produces a list of paths to attributes whose changes mean\n1003: \t// that we must replace rather than update an existing remote object.\n1004: \t// However, we only need to do that if the identified attributes _have_\n1005: \t// actually changed -- particularly after we may have undone some of the\n1006: \t// {\n1010: \t\tfor _, path := range resp.RequiresReplace {\n1011: \t\t\tif priorVal.IsNull() {\n1012: \t\t\t\t// If prior is null then we don't expect any RequiresReplace at all,\n1013: \t\t\t\t// because this is a Create action.\n1014: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1015: \t\t\t}\n1016: \n1017: \t\t\tpriorChangedVal, priorPathDiags := hcl.ApplyPath(unmarkedPriorVal, path, nil)\n1018: \t\t\tplannedChangedVal, plannedPathDiags := hcl.ApplyPath(plannedNewVal, path, nil)\n1019: \t\t\tif plannedPathDiags.HasErrors() && priorPathDiags.HasErrors() {\n1020: \t\t\t\t// This means the path was invalid in both the prior and new\n1021: \t\t\t\t// values, which is an error with the provider itself.\n1022: \t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n1023: \t\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n1024: \t\t\t\t\t\"Provider produced invalid plan\",\n1025: \t\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n1026: \t\t\t\t\t\t\"Provider %q has indicated \\\"requires replacement\\\" on %s for a non-existent attribute path %#v.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n1027: \t\t\t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, n.Addr, path,\n1028: \t\t\t\t\t),\n1029: \t\t\t\t))\n1030: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1031: \t\t\t}\n1032: \n1033: \t\t\t// Make sure we have valid Values for both values.\n1034: \t\t\t// Note: if the opposing value was of the type\n1035: \t\t\t// cty.DynamicPseudoType, the type assigned here may not exactly\n1036: \t\t\t// match the schema. should\n1078: \t\t// prevent us from getting here in that case.\n1079: \t}\n1080: \n1081: \t// Unmark for this test for value equality.\n1082: \teqV := plans.ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason\n1087: \tswitch {\n1088: \tcase priorVal.IsNull():\n1089: \t\taction = plans.Create\n1090: \tcase eq && !matchedForceReplace:\n1091: \t\taction = our filtering above_ then this\n1095: \t\t// is a replace action.\n1096: \t\tif createBeforeDestroy {\n1097: \t\t\taction = plans.CreateThenDelete\n1098: \t\t} else {\n1099: \t\t\taction = \t\t// object's value is not yet complete. }\n1318: \n1319: // Convert the hcl.Traversal values we get form the configuration to the\n1320: // cty.Path values we need to operate on the cty.Values\n1321: func traversalsToPaths(traversals []hcl.Traversal) []cty.Path {\n1322: \tpaths := make([]cty.Path, len(traversals))\n1323: \tfor i, traversal := range traversals {\n1324: \t\tpath := traversalToPath(traversal)\n1325: \t\tpaths[i] = processIgnoreChangesIndividual(prior, config cty.Value, ignoreChangesPath []cty.Path) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1354: \ttype ignoreChange struct {\n1355: \t\t// Path is the full path, minus any trailing map index\n1356: \t\tpath cty.Path\n1357: \t\t// Value is the value we are to retain at the above path. If there is a\n1358: \t\t// key value, this must be a map and the desired value will be at the\n1359: \t\t// key index.\n1360: \t\tvalue cty.Value\n1361: \t\t// Key is the index key if the ignored path ends in a map index.\n1362: \t\tkey cty.Value\n1363: \t}\n1364: \tvar ignoredValues []ignoreChange\n1365: \n1366: \t// Find the actual changes first and store them in the ignoreChange struct.\n1367: \t// If the change was to a map value, and the key doesn't exist in the\n1368: \t// config, it would never be visited in the transform walk.\n1369: \tfor _, icPath := range ignoreChangesPath {\n1370: \t\tkey := cty.NullVal(cty.String)\n1371: \t\t// check for a map index, since maps are the only structure where we\n1372: \t\t// could have invalid path steps.\n1373: \t\tlast, ok := icPath[len(icPath)-1].(cty.IndexStep)\n1374: \t\tif ok {\n1375: \t\t\tif last.Key.Type() == cty.String {\n1376: \t\t\t\ticPath = icPath[:len(icPath)-1]\n1377: \t\t\t\tkey = last.Key\n1378: \t\t\t}\n1379: \t\t}\n1380: \n1381: \t\t// The structure should have been validated already, and we already\n1382: \t\t// trimmed the trailing map index. v\n1495: \t\tdefault:\n1496: \t\t\tnewVal = cty.MapValEmpty(v.Type().ElementType())\n1497: \t\t}\n1498: \n1499: \t\tif len(vMarks) > 0 {\n1500: \t\t\tnewVal = newVal.WithMarks(vMarks)\n1501: \t\t}\n1502: \n1503: \t\treturn newVal, nil\n1504: \t})\n1505: \treturn ret, nil\n1506: }\n1507: \n1508: // readDataSource handles everything needed to call ReadDataSource on the provider.\n1509: // A previously evaluated configVal can be passed in, or a new one is generated\n1510: // from the resource configuration.\n1511: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) readDataSource(ctx EvalContext, configVal cty.Value) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1512: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n1513: \tvar newVal cty.Value\n1514: \n1515: \tconfig := *n.Config\n1516: \n1517: \tprovider, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n1518: \tdiags = diags.Append(err)\n1519: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n1520: \t\treturn newVal, diags\n1521: \t}\n1522: \tschema, _ := providerSchema.SchemaForResourceAddr(n.Addr.ContainingResource().Resource)\n1523: \tif schema == nil {\n1524: \t\t// Should be caught during validation, so we don't bother with a pretty error \t\t\tProviderMeta: metaConfigVal,\n1577: \t\t})\n1578: \t}\n1579: \tdiags = diags.Append(resp.Diagnostics.InConfigBody(config.Config, n.Addr.String()))\n1580: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n1581: \t\treturn newVal, diags\n1582: \t}\n1583: \tnewVal = resp.State\n1584: \tif newVal == cty.NilVal {\n1585: \t\t// This can happen with incompletely-configured mocks. newVal.Type().TestConformance(schema.ImpliedType()) {\n1591: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n1592: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n1593: \t\t\t\"Provider produced invalid object\",\n1594: \t}\n1603: \n1604: \tif newVal.IsNull() {\n1605: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n1606: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n1607: \t\t\t\"Provider produced null object\",\n1608: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n1609: \t\t\t\t\"Provider %q produced a null value for %s.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n1610: \t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider, n.Addr,\n1611: \t\t\t),\n1612: \t\t))\n1613: \t}\n1614: \n1615: \tif !newVal.IsNull() && !newVal.IsWhollyKnown() {\n1616: \t\tdiags = \n1625: \t\t// We'll still save the object, but we need to eliminate any unknown\n1626: \t\t// values first because we can't serialize them in the state file.\n1627: \t\t// Note that this may cause diags.Err())\n1640: \t}))\n1641: \n1642: \treturn newVal, diags\n1643: }\n1644: \n1645: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) providerMetas(ctx EvalContext) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1646: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n1647: \tmetaConfigVal := cty.NullVal(cty.DynamicPseudoType)\n1648: \n1649: \t_, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n1650: \tif err != nil resource lifecycle:\n1674: // either actually reading from the data source or generating a plan to do so.\n1675: //\n1676: // currentState is the current state for the data source, and the new state is\n1677: // returned. While data sources are read-only, we need to start with the prior\n1678: // state to determine if we have a change or not.  If we needed to read a new\n1679: // value, but it still matches the previous state, then we can record a NoNop\n1680: // change. If the states don't match then we record a Read change so that the\n1681: // new value is applied to the state.\n1682: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) planDataSource(ctx EvalContext, checkRuleSeverity tfdiags.Severity, skipPlanChanges bool) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, *states.ResourceInstanceObject, instances.RepetitionData, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1683: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n1684: \tvar keyData instances.RepetitionData\n1685: \tvar configVal cty.Value\n1686: \n1687: \t_, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n1688: \tif err != nil {\n1689: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags.Append(err)\n1690: \t}\n1691: \n1692: \tconfig := *n.Config\n1693: \tschema, _ := providerSchema.SchemaForResourceAddr(n.Addr.ContainingResource().Resource)\n1694: \tif schema == nil {\n1695: \t\t// Should be caught during validation, so we don't bother with a pretty error here\n1696: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(fmt.Errorf(\"provider %q does not support data source %q\", n.ResolvedProvider, n.Addr.ContainingResource().Resource.Type))\n1697: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n1698: \t}\n1699: \n1700: \tobjTy := schema.ImpliedType()\n1701: \tpriorVal := cty.NullVal(objTy)\n1702: \n1703: \tforEach, _ := evaluateForEachExpression(config.ForEach, ctx)\n1704: \tkeyData = EvalDataForInstanceKey(n.ResourceInstanceAddr().Resource.Key, forEach)\n1705: \n1706: \tcheckDiags := evalCheckRules(\n1707: \t\taddrs.ResourcePrecondition,\n1708: \t\tn.Config.Preconditions,\n1709: \t\tctx, n.Addr, keyData,\n1710: \t\tcheckRuleSeverity,\n1711: \t)\n1712: \tdiags = diags.Append(checkDiags)\n1713: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n1714: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags // failed preconditions prevent further evaluation\n1715: \t}\n1716: \n1717: \tvar configDiags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n1718: \tconfigVal, _, configDiags = ctx.EvaluateBlock(config.Config, schema, nil, keyData)\n1719: \tdiags = diags.Append(configDiags)\n1720: \tif configDiags.HasErrors() {\n1721: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n1722: \t}\n1723: \n1724: \tcheck, nested := n.nestedInCheckBlock()\n1725: \tif nested {\n1726: \t\t// Going forward from this point, the only reason we will fail is\n1727: \t\t// that the data source fails to load its data. Normally, this would\n1728: \t\t// cancel the entire plan and this error message would bubble its way\n1729: \t\t// back up to the user.\n1730: \t\t//\n1731: \t\t// But, if we are in a check block then we don't want this data block to\n1732: \t\t// cause the plan to fail. We also need to report a status on the data\n1733: \t\t// block so the check processing later on knows whether to attempt to\n1734: \t\t// process the checks. Either we'll report the data block as failed\n1735: \t\t// if/when we load the data block later, or we want to report it as a\n1736: \t\t// success overall.\n1737: \t\t//\n1738: \t\t// Therefore, we create a deferred function here that will check if the\n1739: \t\t// status for the check has been updated yet, and if not we will set it\n1740: \t\t// to be StatusPass. The rest of this function will only update the\n1741: \t\t// status if it should be StatusFail.\n1742: \t\tdefer func() {\n1743: \t\t\tstatus := ctx.Checks().ObjectCheckStatus(check.Addr().Absolute(n.Addr.Module))\n1744: \t\t\tif status == checks.StatusUnknown {\n1745: \t\t\t\tctx.Checks().ReportCheckResult(check.Addr().Absolute(n.Addr.Module), addrs.CheckDataResource, 0, checks.StatusPass)\n1746: \t\t\t}\n1747: \t\t}()\n1748: \t}\n1749: \n1750: \tconfigKnown := configVal.IsWhollyKnown()\n1751: \tdepsPending := n.dependenciesHavePendingChanges(ctx)\n1752: \t// If our configuration contains any unknown values, or we depend on any\n1753: \t// unknown values then we must defer the read to the apply phase by\n1754: \t// producing a \"Read\" change for this resource, and a placeholder value for\n1755: \t// it in the state.\n1756: \tif depsPending || !configKnown {\n1757: \t\t// We can't plan any changes if we're only refreshing, so the only\n1758: \t\t// value we can set here is whatever was in state previously.\n1759: \t\tif skipPlanChanges {\n1760: \t\t\tplannedNewState := &states.ResourceInstanceObject{\n1761: \t\t\t\tValue:  priorVal,\n1762: \t\t\t\tStatus: states.ObjectReady,\n1763: \t\t\t}\n1764: \n1765: \t\t\treturn nil, plannedNewState, keyData, diags\n1766: \t\t}\n1767: \n1768: \t\tvar reason plans.ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason\n1769: \t\tswitch {\n1770: \t\tcase !configKnown:\n1771: \t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] planDataSource: %s configuration not fully known yet, so deferring to apply phase\", n.Addr)\n1772: \t\t\treason = plans.ResourceInstanceReadBecauseConfigUnknown\n1773: \t\tcase depsPending:\n1774: \t\t\t// NOTE: depsPending can be true at the same time as configKnown\n1775: \t\t\t// is false; configKnown takes precedence because it's more\n1776: \t\t\t// specific.\n1777: \t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] planDataSource: %s configuration is fully known, at least one dependency has changes pending\", n.Addr)\n1778: \t\t\treason = plans.ResourceInstanceReadBecauseDependencyPending\n1779: \t\t}\n1780: \n1781: \t\tunmarkedConfigVal, configMarkPaths := configVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n1782: \t\tproposedNewVal := objchange.PlannedDataResourceObject(schema, unmarkedConfigVal)\n1783: \t\tproposedNewVal = proposedNewVal.MarkWithPaths(configMarkPaths)\n1784: \n1785: \t\t// Apply detects that the data source will need to be read by the After\n1786: \t\t// value containing unknowns from PlanDataResourceObject.\n1787: \t\tplannedChange := &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n1788: \t\t\tAddr:         n.Addr,\n1789: \t\t\tPrevRunAddr:  n.prevRunAddr(ctx),\n1790: \t\t\tProviderAddr: n.ResolvedProvider,\n1791: \t\t\tChange: plans.Change{\n1792: \t\t\t\tAction: plans.Read,\n1793: \t\t\t\tBefore: priorVal,\n1794: \t\t\t\tAfter:  proposedNewVal,\n1795: \t\t\t},\n1796: \t\t\tActionReason: reason,\n1797: \t\t}\n1798: \n1799: \t\tplannedNewState := &states.ResourceInstanceObject{\n1800: \t\t\tValue:  proposedNewVal,\n1801: \t\t\tStatus: states.ObjectPlanned,\n1802: \t\t}\n1803: \n1804: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n1805: \t\t\treturn h.PostDiff(n.Addr, addrs.NotDeposed, plans.Read, priorVal, proposedNewVal)\n1806: \t\t}))\n1807: \n1808: \t\treturn plannedChange, plannedNewState, keyData, diags\n1809: \t}\n1810: \n1811: \t// We have a complete configuration with no dependencies to wait on, so we\n1812: \t// can read the data source into the state.\n1813: \tnewVal, readDiags := n.readDataSource(ctx, configVal)\n1814: \n1815: \t// Now we've loaded the data, and diags tells us whether we were successful\n1816: \t// or not, we are going to create our plannedChange and our\n1817: \t// proposedNewState.\n1818: \tvar plannedChange *plans.ResourceInstanceChange\n1819: \tvar plannedNewState *states.ResourceInstanceObject\n1820: \n1821: \t// If we are a nested block, then we want to create a plannedChange that\n1822: \t// tells \t// disguise that for a nested block. Nested blocks will report the overall\n1826: \t// check as failed but won't affect the rest of the plan operation or block\n1827: \t// an apply operation.\n1828: \n1829: \tif nested {\n1830: \t\taddr := check.Addr().Absolute(n.Addr.Module)\n1831: \n1832: \t\t// Let's fix things up for a nested data block.\n1833: \t\t//\n1834: \t\t// A nested data block doesn't error, and creates a planned change. So,\n1835: \t\t// if we encountered an error we'll tidy up newVal so it makes sense\n1836: \t\t// and handle the error. We'll also create the plannedChange if\n1837: \t\t// appropriate.\n1838: \n1839: \t\tif readDiags.HasErrors() {\n1840: \t\t\t// If we had errors, then we can cover that up by marking the new\n1841: \t\t\t// state as unknown.\n1842: \t\t\tunmarkedConfigVal, configMarkPaths := configVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n1843: \t\t\tnewVal = objchange.PlannedDataResourceObject(schema, unmarkedConfigVal)\n1844: \t\t\tnewVal = newVal.MarkWithPaths(configMarkPaths)\n1845: \n1846: \t\t\t// We still want to report the check as failed even if we are still\n1847: \t\t\t// letting it run again during the apply stage.\n1848: \t\t\tctx.Checks().ReportCheckFailure(addr, addrs.CheckDataResource, 0, readDiags.Err().Error())\n1849: \t\t}\n1850: \n1851: \t\t// Any warning or error diagnostics we'll wrap with some special checks\n1852: \t\t// diagnostics. This is so we can identify them later, and so they'll\n1853: \t\t// only report as warnings.\n1854: \t\treadDiags = tfdiags.OverrideAll(readDiags, tfdiags.Warning, func() tfdiags.DiagnosticExtraWrapper {\n1855: \t\t\treturn &addrs.CheckRuleDiagnosticExtra{\n1856: \t\t\t\tCheckRule: addrs.NewCheckRule(addr, addrs.CheckDataResource, 0),\n1857: \t\t\t}\n1858: \t\t})\n1859: \n1860: \t\tif !skipPlanChanges {\n1861: \t\t\t// refreshOnly plans cannot produce planned changes, so we only do\n1862: \t\t\t// this if skipPlanChanges is false.\n1863: \t\t\tplannedChange = &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n1864: \t\t\t\tAddr:         n.Addr,\n1865: \t\t\t\tPrevRunAddr:  n.prevRunAddr(ctx),\n1866: \t\t\t\tProviderAddr: n.ResolvedProvider,\n1867: \t\t\t\tChange: plans.Change{\n1868: \t\t\t\t\tAction: plans.Read,\n1869: \t\t\t\t\tBefore: priorVal,\n1870: \t\t\t\t\tAfter:  newVal,\n1871: \t\t\t\t},\n1872: \t\t\t\tActionReason: plans.ResourceInstanceReadBecauseCheckNested,\n1873: \t\t\t}\n1874: \t\t}\n1875: \t}\n1876: \n1877: \tdiags = diags.Append(readDiags)\n1878: \tif !diags.HasErrors() {\n1879: \t\t// Finally, let's make our new state.\n1880: \t\tplannedNewState = &states.ResourceInstanceObject{\n1881: \t\t\tValue:  newVal,\n1882: \t\t\tStatus: states.ObjectReady,\n1883: \t\t}\n1884: \t}\n1885: \n1886: \treturn plannedChange, plannedNewState, keyData, diags\n1887: }\n1888: \n1889: // nestedInCheckBlock determines if this resource is nested in a Check config\n1890: // block. If so, this resource will be loaded during both plan and apply\n1891: // operations to make sure the check is always giving the latest information.\n1892: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) nestedInCheckBlock() (*configs.Check, bool) {\n1893: \tif n.Config.Container != nil {\n1894: \t\tcheck, ok := n.Config.Container.(*configs.Check)\n1895: \t\treturn check, ok\n1896: \t}\n1897: \treturn nil, false\n1898: }\n1899: \n1900: // dependenciesHavePendingChanges determines whether any managed resource the\n1901: // receiver depends on has a change pending in the plan, in which case we'd\n1902: // need to override the usual behavior of immediately reading from the data\n1903: // source where possible, and instead defer the read until the apply step.\n1904: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dependenciesHavePendingChanges(ctx EvalContext) bool {\n1905: \tnModInst := n.Addr.Module\n1906: \tnMod := nModInst.Module()\n1907: \n1908: \t// Check and see if any depends_on dependencies have\n1909: \t// changes, since they won't show up as changes in the\n1910: \t// configuration.\n1911: \tchanges := ctx.Changes()\n1912: \n1913: \tdepsToUse := n.dependsOn\n1914: \n1915: \tif n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Mode == addrs.DataResourceMode {\n1916: \t\tif n.Config.HasCustomConditions() {\n1917: \t\t\t// For a data resource with custom conditions we need to look at\n1918: \t\t\t// the full set of resource dependencies -- both direct and\n1919: \t\t\t// indirect -- because an upstream update might be what's needed\n1920: \t\t\t// in order to make a condition pass.\n1921: \t\t\tdepsToUse = n.Dependencies\n1922: \t\t}\n1923: \t}\n1924: \n1925: \tfor _, d := range depsToUse {\n1926: \t\tif d.Resource.Mode == addrs.DataResourceMode {\n1927: \t\t\t// Data sources have no external side effects, so they pose a need\n1928: \t\t\t// to delay this read. If they do have a change planned, it must be\n1929: \t\t\t// because of a dependency on a managed resource, in which case\n1930: \t\t\t// we'll also encounter it in this list of dependencies.\n1931: \t\t\tcontinue\n1932: \t\t}\n1933: \n1934: \t\tfor _, change := range changes.GetChangesForConfigResource(d) {\n1935: \t\t\tchangeModInst := change.Addr.Module\n1936: \t\t\tchangeMod := changeModInst.Module()\n1937: \n1938: \t\t\tif changeMod.Equal(nMod) && !changeModInst.Equal(nModInst) {\n1939: \t\t\t\t// Dependencies are tracked by configuration address, which\n1940: \t\t\t\t// means we may have changes from other instances of parent\n1941: \t\t\t\t// modules. The actual reference can only take effect within\n1942: \t\t\t\t// the same module instance, so skip any that aren't an exact\n1943: \t\t\t\t// match\n1944: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1945: \t\t\t}\n1946: \n1947: \t\t\tif change != nil && change.Action != plans.NoOp {\n1948: \t\t\t\treturn true\n1949: \t\t\t}\n1950: \t\t}\n1951: \t}\n1952: \treturn false\n1953: }\n1954: \n1955: // apply deals with the main part of the data resource lifecycle: either\n1956: // actually reading from the data source or generating a plan to do so.\n1957: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) applyDataSource(ctx EvalContext, planned *plans.ResourceInstanceChange) (*states.ResourceInstanceObject, instances.RepetitionData, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1958: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n1959: \tvar keyData instances.RepetitionData\n1960: \n1961: \t_, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n1962: \tif err != nil {\n1963: \t\treturn nil, keyData, diags.Append(err)\n1964: \t}\n1965: (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) evalApplyProvisioners(ctx EvalContext, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject, createNew bool, when configs.ProvisionerWhen) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n2059: \tvar diags In practice not all remote\\n17: // objects are actually remote in the sense of being accessed over the network,\\n18: // but this is the most common case.\\n19: //\\n20: // It is not valid to mutate a ResourceInstanceObject once it has been created.\\n21: // Instead, create a new object and replace the existing one.\\n22: type ResourceInstanceObject struct {\\n23: \\t// Value is the object-typed value representing the remote object within\\n24: \\t// Terraform.\\n25: \\tValue cty.Value\\n26: \\n27: \\t// Private is an opaque value set by the provider when this object was\\n28: \\t// last created or updated. Terraform Core does not use this value in\\n29: \\t// any way and it is not exposed anywhere in the user interface, so\\n30: \\t// a provider can use it for retaining any necessary private state.\\n31: \\tPrivate []byte\\n32: \\n33: \\t// Status represents the \\\"readiness\\\" of the object as of the last time\\n34: \\t// it was updated.\\n35: \\tStatus ObjectStatus\\n36: \\n37: \\t// Dependencies is a set of absolute address to other resources this\\n38: \\t// instance dependeded on when it was applied. Since it cannot be moved into the\\n64: \\t// ObjectRead state, a tainted object must be replaced.\\n65: \\tObjectTainted ObjectStatus = 'T'\\n66: \\n67: \\t// ObjectPlanned is a special object status used only for the transient\\n68: \\t// placeholder objects we place into state during the refresh and plan\\n69: \\t// walks to stand in for objects that will be created during apply.\\n70: \\t//\\n71: \\t// Any object of this status must have a corresponding change recorded\\n72: \\t// in the current plan, whose value must then be used in preference to\\n73: \\t// the value stored in state when evaluating expressions. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01L1nyFsrVfKJHtiKUTbmXyt","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01H75T3fyMVeLxEhAewkBG8o","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Investigation Report: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes in Terraform\n\n## Summary\n\nTerraform generates phantom in-place update changes for resources with provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes because of an **asymmetry between how sensitivity marks are applied during refresh and how they are compared during planning**. The refresh path re-applies only marks from the prior state (excluding schema-defined marks), while the plan comparison checks for mark equality without accounting for the schema-defined marks that should be present on the planned value.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe root cause is a **multi-layer sensitivity mark gap** spanning four packages:\n\n1. **Graph Evaluation Layer** (`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`): Provider responses are processed without schema-defined sensitive marks\n2. **State Serialization Layer** (`internal/states/instance_object.go`): State storage only preserves marks that were already on the value, missing schema-defined marks\n3. **Plan Comparison Layer** (`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`): The mark comparison uses incomplete mark sets\n4. **Expression Evaluation Layer** (`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`): Compensating workaround that applies schema marks only for expression evaluation, creating asymmetry\n\n## Evidence\n\n### 1. Provider Response Processing (Refresh Path)\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:619-723`\n\nThe `refresh()` method receives an unmarked provider response and re-applies marks from the prior state:\n\n```go\n// Line 620-626: Extract marks from prior state\npriorVal := state.Value\nvar priorPaths []cty.PathValueMarks\nif priorVal.ContainsMarked() {\n    priorVal, priorPaths = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n}\n\n// Line 636-642: Provider returns unmarked value\nresp = provider.ReadResource(providers.ReadResourceRequest{\n    TypeName:     n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n    PriorState:   priorVal,\n    ...\n})\n\n// Line 718-720: Re-apply only prior marks to new value\nif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n    ret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n}\n```\n\n**Critical Issue**: `priorPaths` contains only marks that were stored in state. Schema-defined sensitive attributes are NOT stored in state because the value never had those marks applied before encoding.\n\n### 2. State Serialization (Incomplete Sensitivity Recording)\n\n**File:** `internal/states/instance_object.go:94-137`\n\nThe `Encode()` method removes all marks and stores only those that were present:\n\n```go\n// Line 98: Unmark the value and extract mark paths\nval, pvm := o.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n\n// Line 131: Store only the extracted marks\nreturn &ResourceInstanceObjectSrc{\n    AttrSensitivePaths:  pvm,  // Only marks that were on the value\n    ...\n}\n```\n\n**Critical Issue**: `pvm` (PathValueMarks) contains only marks that were on the value. Schema-defined sensitive attributes from the provider schema are never marked ON the value during refresh, so they are not included in `AttrSensitivePaths` stored in the state file.\n\nThe state file's `sensitive_attributes` section reflects incomplete sensitivity:\n- ✅ Includes marks from variable references (e.g., `var.db_password` marked sensitive)\n- ❌ Excludes schema-defined sensitive paths (e.g., `password` attribute with `Sensitive: true`)\n\n### 3. Plan Comparison (Mark Asymmetry)\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:868-1208`\n\nThe `plan()` method extracts marks from config and prior state, then compares them:\n\n```go\n// Line 868-869: Extract marks from configuration and prior state\nunmarkedConfigVal, unmarkedPaths := configValIgnored.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\nunmarkedPriorVal, priorPaths := priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n\n// Line 998-1000: Re-apply configuration marks to planned value\nif len(unmarkedPaths) > 0 {\n    plannedNewVal = plannedNewVal.MarkWithPaths(unmarkedPaths)\n}\n\n// Line 1018: Compare for RequiresReplace filtering\nplannedChangedVal, plannedPathDiags := hcl.ApplyPath(plannedNewVal, path, nil)\n\n// Line 1208: Convert NoOp to Update if marks differ\nif action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n    action = plans.Update\n}\n```\n\n**Critical Issue**:\n- `unmarkedPaths` contains only marks from the configuration (sensitive variable references)\n- `priorPaths` contains only marks from prior state (excluding schema-defined marks)\n- The comparison at line 1208 detects a difference because the planned value has configuration marks but the prior value doesn't have schema marks\n- Since the underlying VALUES are identical (confirmed by line 1082), the diff is ONLY in sensitivity metadata\n\nThis causes the phantom in-place update even though `eqV.True()` at line 1083 would show no value changes.\n\n### 4. Compensating Workaround (Asymmetric Application)\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/evaluate.go:689-723`\n\nThe expression evaluator applies schema-defined sensitive marks ONLY when reading resources for evaluation:\n\n```go\n// Line 689-695: Applied during planned value expression evaluation\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    afterMarks = append(afterMarks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)\n}\ninstances[key] = val.MarkWithPaths(afterMarks)\n\n// Line 714-723: Applied during current state expression evaluation\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    var marks []cty.PathValueMarks\n    val, marks = val.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)\n    val = val.MarkWithPaths(marks)\n}\ninstances[key] = val\n```\n\n**Critical Issue**: This compensating workaround is applied ONLY in the expression evaluator (`GetResource()`) when resources are read for evaluating HCL expressions. It does NOT apply to:\n- Values during the plan comparison phase (line 1208)\n- Values during state refresh (line 719)\n- Values stored in state\n\nThis creates an asymmetry where:\n- Values FOR EVALUATION are marked with schema-defined sensitivity\n- Values FOR COMPARISON and STORAGE are NOT marked with schema-defined sensitivity\n\n### 5. JSON Output Manifestation\n\n**File:** `internal/command/jsonstate/state.go:402-406`\n\nWhen generating `terraform show -json` output, the code applies schema marks to generate accurate sensitivity metadata:\n\n```go\n// Line 402-406: Schema marks ARE applied for JSON output\nvalue, marks := riObj.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(value, nil)...)\n}\ns := SensitiveAsBool(value.MarkWithPaths(marks))\nv, err := ctyjson.Marshal(s, s.Type())\n```\n\nHowever, this happens AFTER the state was already serialized without schema marks. The `sensitive_values` section in JSON output appears more complete than `sensitive_attributes` in the actual state file because this code layer applies marks during DISPLAY, not during STORAGE.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`** (Graph Evaluation)\n   - `refresh()`: Lines 619-723 - Doesn't apply schema marks to refreshed state\n   - `plan()`: Lines 868-1208 - Compares marks without schema-defined sensitivity\n\n2. **`internal/states/instance_object.go`** (State Serialization)\n   - `Encode()`: Lines 94-137 - Stores incomplete sensitivity marks\n\n3. **`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`** (State Deserialization)\n   - `Decode()`: Lines 77-104 - Applies stored marks without schema marks\n\n4. **`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`** (Expression Evaluation - Compensation Only)\n   - `GetResource()`: Lines 689-695, 714-723 - Applies schema marks for evaluation only\n\n5. **`internal/command/jsonstate/state.go`** (JSON Output)\n   - `marshalResources()`: Lines 402-406, 453-456 - Applies schema marks during display\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Provider Response** → Provider returns unmarked value (providers don't mark values)\n2. **Refresh Processing** → `refresh()` re-applies only prior-state marks (schema marks were never stored)\n3. **State Encoding** → `Encode()` stores only marks on the value (excludes schema marks)\n4. **State Storage** → State file has incomplete `sensitive_attributes`\n5. **State Decoding** → `Decode()` applies stored marks (still missing schema marks)\n6. **Plan Extraction** → `plan()` extracts `priorPaths` from decoded state (missing schema marks)\n7. **Plan Comparison** → Mark equality check finds difference between `plannedNewVal` (has config marks) and `priorVal` (missing schema marks)\n8. **Phantom Update** → Line 1208 converts `NoOp` to `Update` due to mark inequality despite value equality\n9. **JSON Display** → `jsonstate.marshalResources()` applies schema marks for display, showing accurate sensitivity in JSON but incomplete in state file\n\n## Recommendation\n\nThe fix requires ensuring schema-defined sensitive paths are present in the marks throughout the pipeline:\n\n### Option A (Preferred): Apply Schema Marks at Source\n- **When**: During `refresh()` at line 718, after retrieving the provider response\n- **Where**: In `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`\n- **How**: After line 718, apply schema-defined marks using `schema.ValueMarks()` before storing the value\n- **Benefit**: Ensures schema marks flow through the entire pipeline consistently\n\n### Option B: Store Schema Marks During Encoding\n- **When**: In `Encode()` before storing state\n- **Where**: In `internal/states/instance_object.go:94-137`\n- **How**: Before encoding, append schema-defined marks to the extracted marks\n- **Benefit**: Ensures state file records complete sensitivity information\n- **Challenge**: Requires access to provider schema during state encoding, which isn't currently available\n\n### Option C: Apply Schema Marks During Plan Comparison\n- The refresh path re-applies only marks from the prior state (excluding schema-defined marks), while the plan comparison checks for mark equality without accounting for the schema-defined marks that should be present on the planned value.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe root cause is a **multi-layer sensitivity mark gap** spanning four packages:\n\n1. **Graph Evaluation Layer** (`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`): Provider responses are processed without schema-defined sensitive marks\n2. **State Serialization Layer** (`internal/states/instance_object.go`): State storage only preserves marks that were already on the value, missing schema-defined marks\n3. **Plan Comparison Layer** (`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`): The mark comparison uses incomplete mark sets\n4. **Expression Evaluation Layer** (`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`): Compensating workaround that applies schema marks only for expression evaluation, creating asymmetry\n\n## Evidence\n\n### 1. Provider Response Processing (Refresh Path)\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:619-723`\n\nThe `refresh()` method receives an unmarked provider response and re-applies marks from the prior state:\n\n```go\n// Line 620-626: Extract marks from prior state\npriorVal := state.Value\nvar priorPaths []cty.PathValueMarks\nif priorVal.ContainsMarked() {\n    priorVal, priorPaths = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n}\n\n// Line 636-642: Provider returns unmarked value\nresp = provider.ReadResource(providers.ReadResourceRequest{\n    TypeName:     n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n    PriorState:   priorVal,\n    ...\n})\n\n// Line 718-720: Re-apply only prior marks to new value\nif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n    ret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n}\n```\n\n**Critical Issue**: `priorPaths` contains only marks that were stored in state. Schema-defined sensitive attributes are NOT stored in state because the value never had those marks applied before encoding.\n\n### 2. State Serialization (Incomplete Sensitivity Recording)\n\n**File:** `internal/states/instance_object.go:94-137`\n\nThe `Encode()` method removes all marks and stores only those that were present:\n\n```go\n// Line 98: Unmark the value and extract mark paths\nval, pvm := o.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n\n// Line 131: Store only the extracted marks\nreturn &ResourceInstanceObjectSrc{\n    AttrSensitivePaths:  pvm,  // Only marks that were on the value\n    ...\n}\n```\n\n**Critical Issue**: `pvm` (PathValueMarks) contains only marks that were on the value. Schema-defined sensitive attributes from the provider schema are never marked ON the value during refresh, so they are not included in `AttrSensitivePaths` stored in the state file.\n\nThe state file's `sensitive_attributes` section reflects incomplete sensitivity:\n- ✅ Includes marks from variable references (e.g., `var.db_password` marked sensitive)\n- ❌ Excludes schema-defined sensitive paths (e.g., `password` attribute with `Sensitive: true`)\n\n### 3. Plan Comparison (Mark Asymmetry)\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:868-1208`\n\nThe `plan()` method extracts marks from config and prior state, then compares them:\n\n```go\n// Line 868-869: Extract marks from configuration and prior state\nunmarkedConfigVal, unmarkedPaths := configValIgnored.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\nunmarkedPriorVal, priorPaths := priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n\n// Line 998-1000: Re-apply configuration marks to planned value\nif len(unmarkedPaths) > 0 {\n    plannedNewVal = plannedNewVal.MarkWithPaths(unmarkedPaths)\n}\n\n// Line 1018: Compare for RequiresReplace filtering\nplannedChangedVal, plannedPathDiags := hcl.ApplyPath(plannedNewVal, path, nil)\n\n// Line 1208: Convert NoOp to Update if marks differ\nif action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n    action = plans.Update\n}\n```\n\n**Critical Issue**:\n- `unmarkedPaths` contains only marks from the configuration (sensitive variable references)\n- `priorPaths` contains only marks from prior state (excluding schema-defined marks)\n- The comparison at line 1208 detects a difference because the planned value has configuration marks but the prior value doesn't have schema marks\n- Since the underlying VALUES are identical (confirmed by line 1082), the diff is ONLY in sensitivity metadata\n\nThis causes the phantom in-place update even though `eqV.True()` at line 1083 would show no value changes.\n\n### 4. Compensating Workaround (Asymmetric Application)\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/evaluate.go:689-723`\n\nThe expression evaluator applies schema-defined sensitive marks ONLY when reading resources for evaluation:\n\n```go\n// Line 689-695: Applied during planned value expression evaluation\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    afterMarks = append(afterMarks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)\n}\ninstances[key] = val.MarkWithPaths(afterMarks)\n\n// Line 714-723: Applied during current state expression evaluation\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    var marks []cty.PathValueMarks\n    val, marks = val.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)\n    val = val.MarkWithPaths(marks)\n}\ninstances[key] = val\n```\n\n**Critical Issue**: This compensating workaround is applied ONLY in the expression evaluator (`GetResource()`) when resources are read for evaluating HCL expressions. It does NOT apply to:\n- Values during the plan comparison phase (line 1208)\n- Values during state refresh (line 719)\n- Values stored in state\n\nThis creates an asymmetry where:\n- Values FOR EVALUATION are marked with schema-defined sensitivity\n- Values FOR COMPARISON and STORAGE are NOT marked with schema-defined sensitivity\n\n### 5. JSON Output Manifestation\n\n**File:** `internal/command/jsonstate/state.go:402-406`\n\nWhen generating `terraform show -json` output, the code applies schema marks to generate accurate sensitivity metadata:\n\n```go\n// Line 402-406: Schema marks ARE applied for JSON output\nvalue, marks := riObj.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(value, nil)...)\n}\ns := SensitiveAsBool(value.MarkWithPaths(marks))\nv, err := ctyjson.Marshal(s, s.Type())\n```\n\nHowever, this happens AFTER the state was already serialized without schema marks. The `sensitive_values` section in JSON output appears more complete than `sensitive_attributes` in the actual state file because this code layer applies marks during DISPLAY, not during STORAGE.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`** (Graph Evaluation)\n   - `refresh()`: Lines 619-723 - Doesn't apply schema marks to refreshed state\n   - `plan()`: Lines 868-1208 - Compares marks without schema-defined sensitivity\n\n2. **`internal/states/instance_object.go`** (State Serialization)\n   - `Encode()`: Lines 94-137 - Stores incomplete sensitivity marks\n\n3. **`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`** (State Deserialization)\n   - `Decode()`: Lines 77-104 - Applies stored marks without schema marks\n\n4. **`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`** (Expression Evaluation - Compensation Only)\n   - `GetResource()`: Lines 689-695, 714-723 - Applies schema marks for evaluation only\n\n5. **`internal/command/jsonstate/state.go`** (JSON Output)\n   - `marshalResources()`: Lines 402-406, 453-456 - Applies schema marks during display\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Provider Response** → Provider returns unmarked value (providers don't mark values)\n2. **Refresh Processing** → `refresh()` re-applies only prior-state marks (schema marks were never stored)\n3. **State Encoding** → `Encode()` stores only marks on the value (excludes schema marks)\n4. **State Storage** → State file has incomplete `sensitive_attributes`\n5. **State Decoding** → `Decode()` applies stored marks (still missing schema marks)\n6. **Plan Extraction** → `plan()` extracts `priorPaths` from decoded state (missing schema marks)\n7. **Plan Comparison** → Mark equality check finds difference between `plannedNewVal` (has config marks) and `priorVal` (missing schema marks)\n8. **Phantom Update** → Line 1208 converts `NoOp` to `Update` due to mark inequality despite value equality\n9. **JSON Display** → `jsonstate.marshalResources()` applies schema marks for display, showing accurate sensitivity in JSON but incomplete in state file\n\n## Recommendation\n\nThe fix requires ensuring schema-defined sensitive paths are present in the marks throughout the pipeline:\n\n### Option A (Preferred): Apply Schema Marks at Source\n- **When**: During `refresh()` at line 718, after retrieving the provider response\n- **Where**: In `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`\n- **How**: After line 718, apply schema-defined marks using `schema.ValueMarks()` before storing the value\n- **Benefit**: Ensures schema marks flow through the entire pipeline consistently\n\n### Option B: Store Schema Marks During Encoding\n- **When**: In `Encode()` before storing state\n- **Where**: In `internal/states/instance_object.go:94-137`\n- **How**: Before encoding, append schema-defined marks to the extracted marks\n- **Benefit**: Ensures state file records complete sensitivity information\n- **Challenge**: Requires access to provider schema during state encoding, which isn't currently available\n\n### Option C: Apply Schema Marks During Plan Comparison\n- **When**: In `plan()` before the mark equality check at line 1208\n- **Where**: In `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208`\n- **How**: Augment both `plannedNewVal` marks and `priorPaths` with schema marks before comparison\n- **Benefit**: Targeted fix that only affects plan phase\n- **Challenge**: Still leaves state storage incomplete\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n1. Compare `AttrSensitivePaths` in state file for resources with schema-defined sensitive attributes—should include full paths\n2.
